Al-Khaliq, al-Bari', and al-Musawwir: Distinct Stages of Creation
al-Ghazali distinguishes three stages of creation using the names al-Khaliq, al-Bari', and al-Musawwir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that al-Khaliq, al-Bari', and al-Musawwir are not synonymous but denote distinct stages of divine creation: estimation, bringing into existence, and forming.

Core Idea
Creation involves three distinct acts: planning, making, and beautifying.

This passage from al-Ghazali clarifies a common confusion about three divine names: al-Khaliq, al-Bari', and al-Musawwir. Many think they are synonyms, but al-Ghazali shows they refer to sequential stages in the creative process. By understanding this distinction, you gain a deeper appreciation of the precision of divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the passage carefully, noting the three names and the analogy of the building.
2
Identify the three stages
Al-Ghazali lists three requirements for bringing something from non-existence: taqdir, ijad, taswir. Map each to a name.
3
Reflect on the analogy
Consider how the engineer, builder, and painter illustrate the distinct roles. Why is this important for understanding God's attributes?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخالق البارئ معناهما واحد أي المختص باختراع الأشياء ( المصور المختص بإحداث الصور) المختلفة ( والتراكيب ( المتفاوتة فهذه الأسماء الثلاثة صفات من الفعل، قال الغزالي رحمه الله : قد يظن أن هذه الثلاثة مترادفة وأنها راجعة إلى الخلق والاختراع والأولى أن يقال : ما يخرج من العدم إلى الوجود يحتاج أولاً إلى التقدير وثانياً إلى الإيجاد على وفق ذلك التقدير، وثالثاً التصوير والتزيين كالبناء بقدرة المهندس ثم يبنيه الباني ثم يزينه النقاش. فالله سبحانه خالق من حيث أنه مقدر،
Al-Khaliq and al-Bari' have the same meaning, i.e., the one specialized in inventing things. Al-Musawwir is the one specialized in producing different forms and diverse compositions. So these three names are attributes of action. Al-Ghazali, may Allah have mercy on him, said: It may be thought that these three are synonymous and that they return to creation and invention, but the better view is to say: What comes out of non-existence into existence requires first estimation (taqdir), second bringing into existence (ijad) according to that estimation, and third forming and adorning (taswir wa tazyin), like a building by the power of the engineer, then the builder builds it, then the painter decorates it. So Allah, glorified, is Khaliq (Creator) in that He is the Estimator.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage is a classification and distinction of the divine names al-Khaliq, al-Bari', and al-Musawwir. The author first notes that al-Khaliq and al-Bari' are often taken as synonyms meaning the one who invents things, while al-Musawwir specifically produces forms and compositions. These are all attributes of action. Then he quotes al-Ghazali, who warns against thinking they are mere synonyms. Instead, al-Ghazali explains that bringing something from non-existence to existence involves three stages: (1) estimation or planning (taqdir) – this is the role of al-Khaliq; (2) actual bringing into existence (ijad) according to that plan – this is al-Bari'; and (3) forming and adorning (taswir) – this is al-Musawwir. An analogy is given of a building: the engineer estimates, the builder constructs, and the painter decorates. Thus, each name highlights a distinct divine act. The passage emphasizes that these names are not redundant but convey different aspects of God's creative power.

إيجاد
تصوير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Khaliq, al-Bari', and al-Musawwir are synonyms meaning the same thing.
Correction: While al-Khaliq and al-Bari' are synonyms, al-Musawwir is distinct. More precisely, al-Ghazali shows they each refer to a different stage in creation.

Checkpoint
According to al-Ghazali's explanation, which name corresponds to the stage of 'estimation' (taqdir) in creation?
A) al-Khaliq
B) al-Bari'
C) al-Musawwir
D) All three equally

Key Takeaway
Al-Khaliq, al-Bari', and al-Musawwir represent three sequential divine acts: estimation, bringing into existence, and forming.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you witness a beautiful sunset or a newborn baby, do you consciously reflect on the three distinct stages of God's creation—estimation, bringing into existence, and forming? Which stage do you most often neglect, and how can you train yourself to see all three in everyday life?
?
Al-Ghazali compares God to an engineer, a builder, and a painter. In your own life, do you trust that God has already 'estimated' every detail of your future? How does recalling His role as al-Khaliq (the Estimator) change the way you face uncertainty?
?
If creation is not a single act but a sequence of deliberate divine actions, what does that say about the value and purpose of everything around you? How should this understanding affect your gratitude and your treatment of God's creation?

Meanings of al-Aziz (العزيز)
Al-Jurjani enumerates several interpretations of al-Aziz, classifying them into negative or active attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the various interpretations of the divine name al-Aziz and how they relate to different types of attributes (negative and active).

Core Idea
Al-Aziz can be understood as a negation of deficiency or as an active attribute of power.

Al-Jurjani begins his discussion of the divine names with al-Aziz, presenting a range of linguistic and theological interpretations. This passage shows how scholars derive different attribute types from the same word, depending on the nuance emphasized.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on al-Aziz carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the multiple 'qīl' (it is said) statements.
2
Identify the different interpretations
List each interpretation mentioned. There are several: negation of parenthood, being lowered, being unattainable, no likeness, tormenting/rewarding, and power.
3
Classify each interpretation
For each interpretation, note whether the commentator classifies it as a negative attribute (sifa salbiyya) or an active attribute (sifa fi'liyya). Understand the reasoning.
Most interpretations are negative, but some are active.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد السابع - المقصد الثالث : تسميته تعالى بالاسماء توفيقية
وسيأتي معناه: العزيز قيل: معناه لا أب له ولا أم، وقيل: لا يحط عن منزلته، ويقرب من هذا تفسيره بالذي لا يرام أو الذي لا يخالف أو الذي لا يخوف بالتهديد، وقيل: لا مثل له، وهو بهذا المعنى وبالمعنى الأول مشتق من عز الشيء يعز بالكسر في المستقبل إذا لم يكن له نظير، ومنه عز الطعام في البلد إذا تعذر، وحاصل الكل يرجع إلى صفة سلبية. وقيل: يعذب من أراد، وقيل: عليه ثواب العاملين، فيرجع إلى صفة فعلية هي التعذيب أو الإثابة. وقيل: القادر، والعزة القدرة والغلبة. ومنه المثل: من عز، أي من قدر وغلب سلب. الجبار: قيل: من الجبر بمعنى الإصلاح، أي المصلح لأمور الخلائق فإنه جابر كل كسير، ومنه جبر العظم أي أصلحه. وقيل: من الجبر بمعنى الإكراه، يقال: جبره السلطان على كذا وأجبره إذا أكرهه، أي يجبر خلقه ويحملهم على ما يريده، فمرجعه على المعنيين صفة فعلية. وقيل: معناه منيع لا ينال، فإنه سبحانه وتعالى متعال عن أن تناله يد الأفكار أو يحيط به إدراك الأبصار، ومنه نخلة جبارة إذا طالت وقصرت الأيدي عن أن تنال أعلاها، فمرجعه إلى صفة إضافية مع سلبية. وقيل: لا يبالي بما كان وبما لم يكن، وقد يعبر عن هذا المعنى بأنه إذا لا يتمنى ما لا يكون ولا يلتهف على ما لم يكن، فمرجعه إلى الصفات السلبية. وقيل: هو العظيم، هكذا نقل عن ابن عباس، ثم فسر المصنف العظيم بقوله: أي انتفت عنه صفات النقص، فمرجعه صفة سلبية. وقيل: أي انتفى عنه تلك الصفات وحصل له جميع صفات الكمال، فيرجع إلى الصفات السلبية والثبوتية معاً. المتكبر: قيل في معناه ما قيل في معنى العظيم. وقال الغزالي رحمه الله: المتكبر المطلق هو الذي الكل يرى حقيراً بالإضافة إلى ذاته، فإن كانت هذه الرؤية صادقة كان التكبر حقاً وصاحبه محقاً، ولا ذلك على الإطلاق إلا الله، وإن كانت كاذبة كان التكبر باطلاً والمتكبر مبطلاً. الخالق البارئ معناهما واحد: أي المختص باختراع الأشياء. المصور: المختص بإحداث الصور المختلفة والتراكيب المتفاوتة، فهذه الأسماء الثلاثة صفات من الفعل. قال الغزالي رحمه الله: قد يظن أن هذه الثلاثة مترادفة وأنها راجعة إلى الخلق والاختراع، والأولى أن يقال: ما يخرج من العدم إلى الوجود يحتاج أولاً إلى التقدير، وثانياً إلى الإيجاد على وفق ذلك التقدير، وثالثاً التصوير والتزيين، كالبناء بقدرة المهندس ثم يبنيه الباني ثم يزينه النقاش. فالله سبحانه خالق من حيث أنه مقدر، وبارئ من حيث أنه موجد، ومصور من حيث أنه يرتب صور المخترعات أحسن ترتيب ويزينها أكمل تزيين.
The Seventh Observatory - The Third Objective: His naming (Exalted is He) with the names is tawfīqī (subject to divine prescription). And its meaning will come: al-‘Azīz (the Almighty) – it is said: its meaning is that He has no father nor mother, and it is said: He is not lowered from His station. And close to this is its interpretation as the one who is not attained, or the one who does not oppose, or the one who does not frighten with threat. And it is said: there is no likeness to Him. And with this meaning and with the first meaning, it is derived from ‘azza al-shay’ ya‘izzu (in the future, with kasra) when it has no peer. And from this is the scarcity of food in the country when it becomes difficult. And the sum of all returns to a negative attribute (ṣifa salbiyya). And it is said: He torments whomever He wills, and it is said: upon Him is the reward of the doers of good, so it returns to an active attribute (ṣifa fi‘liyya) which is torment or reward. And it is said: al-Qādir (the Powerful), and al-‘izza is power and dominance. And from this is the proverb: 'man ‘azza' – i.e., whoever prevails and dominates, overwhelms. Al-Jabbār (the Compeller): it is said: from jabr meaning reform – i.e., the One who reforms the affairs of creatures, for He is the One who joins every broken thing; and from this is 'setting a bone' – i.e., He repaired it. And it is said: from jabr meaning coercion – it is said: the ruler compelled him to such-and-such and forced him when he overpowered him – i.e., He compels His creatures and forces them to what He wills. So its reference on both meanings is an active attribute. And it is said: its meaning is inapproachable, unattainable – for He, glorified and exalted, is too exalted for the hand of thoughts to reach Him or the perception of sights to encompass Him. And from this is a tall palm tree (jabbāra) when it is long and hands fall short of reaching its top. So its reference is to an additive attribute (ṣifa idāfiyya) combined with a negative one. And it is said: He does not care about what has been and what has not been. And this meaning is sometimes expressed as that He does not wish for what is not and does not regret what has not been. So its reference is to the negative attributes. And it is said: He is al-‘Aẓīm (the Magnificent) – thus transmitted from Ibn ‘Abbās. Then the author interpreted al-‘Aẓīm by his saying: i.e., the attributes of deficiency are negated from Him, so its reference is a negative attribute. And it is said: i.e., those attributes are negated from Him and all attributes of perfection obtain for Him, so it returns to the negative and positive attributes together. Al-Mutakabbir (the Majestic): it is said in its meaning what was said in the meaning of al-‘Aẓīm. And al-Ghazālī (may Allah have mercy on him) said: The absolutely Majestic is the one in relation to whose essence everything sees itself as insignificant. If this vision is true, then the majesty is true and its possessor is truthful, and this is not absolutely except for Allah. And if it is false, then the majesty is false and the one claiming it is a liar. Al-Khāliq (the Creator) and al-Bāri’ (the Maker): their meaning is one – i.e., the One specifically characterized by inventing things. Al-Muṣawwir (the Fashioner): the One specifically characterized by producing the various forms and different compositions. So these three names are attributes of act. Al-Ghazālī (may Allah have mercy on him) said: It may be thought that these three are synonymous and that they refer to creation and invention. But the better way is to say: That which comes from non-existence into existence needs firstly estimation (taqdīr), secondly bringing into existence (ījād) in accordance with that estimation, and thirdly forming and adorning (taṣwīr and tazyīn), like a building by the capability of the engineer, then the builder builds it, then the decorator decorates it. So Allah, glorified, is Khāliq (Creator) in that He is the Estimer (muqaddir), and Bāri’ (Maker) in that He is the Bringer-into-existence (mūjid), and Muṣawwir (Fashioner) in that He arranges the forms of created things in the best arrangement and adorns them with the most complete adornment.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage is a lexical and theological commentary on several divine names, explaining their meanings and classifying the resulting attributes. The commentator begins with the name al-‘Azīz (the Almighty). He presents multiple linguistic interpretations: some take it as negation of parenthood or being lowered, others as invincibility or incomparability. He traces its derivation from ‘izzah (might) and notes that most interpretations lead to a negative attribute (ṣifa salbiyya), i.e., negating deficiency, though one interpretation (relating to rewarding or tormenting) makes it an active attribute (ṣifa fi‘liyya). He also mentions the view that it means al-Qādir (the Powerful), connecting ‘izzah to power and dominance. Next, he treats al-Jabbār (the Compeller) with two main interpretations: one from jabr as reform (the Restorer of broken things), and another from jabr as coercion (the One who compels creatures to His will). Both yield an active attribute. A third interpretation makes it negative (inapproachable), and a fourth makes it an additive-negative attribute. He also connects it to al-‘Aẓīm (the Magnificent) via Ibn ‘Abbās, which the author (al-Jurjānī) takes as a negative attribute or combined negative-positive. For al-Mutakabbir (the Majestic), he echoes the meaning of al-‘Aẓīm and adds al-Ghazālī’s explanation: absolute majesty is only true for Allah, as everything else is truly insignificant in relation to Him. Finally, he discusses three names: al-Khāliq (Creator), al-Bāri’ (Maker), and al-Muṣawwir (Fashioner). He notes they are active attributes and cites al-Ghazālī to differentiate them: creation involves three stages—estimation (taqdīr), bringing into existence (ījād), and forming/adornment (taṣwīr). Thus, al-Khāliq is the Estimator, al-Bāri’ is the Bringer-into-existence, and al-Muṣawwir is the Fashioner of forms in the best manner. This passage shows the careful attention to linguistic roots and theological categories in defining the divine names.

Key Terms
العزيز
صفة سلبية
صفة فعلية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think al-‘Azīz only refers to power (active attribute) and not to negation.
Correction: The passage shows that many interpretations are negative, negating any imperfection or peer.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT listed as a possible meaning of al-‘Azīz?
A) He has no father or mother.
B) He is not lowered from His station.
C) He compels His creatures.
D) He torments whom He wills.

Key Takeaway
The name al-‘Azīz can be interpreted in multiple ways, primarily as a negation of deficiency or as an active attribute of power, reflecting the richness of the Arabic language.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a situation where you feel weak or threatened, how will the knowledge that Allah's al-Aziz includes both the negation of any deficiency and the active power to overcome change your response? What specific reminder will you set for yourself tomorrow?
?
The passage shows that the same name can be understood in multiple ways. Are you willing to expand your understanding of Allah's attributes beyond your comfortable interpretations, even if it means confronting deeper meanings that challenge your assumptions? What concrete step will you take this week to study one more attribute in this way?
?
You have read that al-Aziz can mean 'no peer' and 'powerful'. Which of these meanings do you need to internalize today to deepen your tawakkul? Write down one specific situation where you will live out that meaning.

Meanings of al-Jabbar (الجبار)
Al-Jurjani presents four types of interpretations for al-Jabbar, each leading to a different attribute classification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the different interpretations of al-Jabbar (the Compeller) and how they relate to active, negative, and additive attributes.

Core Idea
Al-Jabbar can mean the Restorer, the Compeller, the Inapproachable, or the Magnificent, each leading to a different attribute category.

Following al-Aziz, Al-Jurjani examines al-Jabbar, presenting multiple interpretations that range from reform and coercion to inapproachability and grandeur. This passage illustrates how the same divine name can be analyzed linguistically and theologically to yield distinct attribute classifications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on al-Jabbar carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice the multiple 'qīl' statements.
Pay attention to the root 'j-b-r' and its two meanings.
2
Identify the four interpretations
List the interpretations: (1) jabr as reform, (2) jabr as coercion, (3) inapproachable, (4) al-‘Aẓīm. Note the sub-variations.
3
Classify each interpretation
For each, note the attribute classification: active (sifa fi‘liyya), additive-negative (sifa idāfiyya ma‘a salbiyya), negative (salbiyya), or combined negative-positive.
The author's comments guide the classification.

المصور: المختص بإحداث الصور المختلفة والتراكيب المتفاوتة، فهذه الأسماء الثلاثة صفات من الفعل. قال الغزالي رحمه الله: قد يظن أن هذه الثلاثة مترادفة وأنها راجعة إلى الخلق والاختراع، والأولى أن يقال: ما يخرج من العدم إلى الوجود يحتاج أولاً إلى التقدير، وثانياً إلى الإيجاد على وفق ذلك التقدير، وثالثاً التصوير والتزيين، كالبناء بقدرة المهندس ثم يبنيه الباني ثم يزينه النقاش. فالله سبحانه خالق من حيث أنه مقدر، وبارئ من حيث أنه موجد، ومصور من حيث أنه يرتب صور المخترعات أحسن ترتيب ويزينها أكمل تزيين.
The Seventh Observatory - The Third Objective: His naming (Exalted is He) with the names is tawfīqī (subject to divine prescription). And its meaning will come: al-‘Azīz (the Almighty) – it is said: its meaning is that He has no father nor mother, and it is said: He is not lowered from His station. And close to this is its interpretation as the one who is not attained, or the one who does not oppose, or the one who does not frighten with threat. And it is said: there is no likeness to Him. And with this meaning and with the first meaning, it is derived from ‘azza al-shay’ ya‘izzu (in the future, with kasra) when it has no peer. And from this is the scarcity of food in the country when it becomes difficult. And the sum of all returns to a negative attribute (ṣifa salbiyya). And it is said: He torments whomever He wills, and it is said: upon Him is the reward of the doers of good, so it returns to an active attribute (ṣifa fi‘liyya) which is torment or reward. And it is said: al-Qādir (the Powerful), and al-‘izza is power and dominance. And from this is the proverb: 'man ‘azza' – i.e., whoever prevails and dominates, overwhelms. Al-Jabbār (the Compeller): it is said: from jabr meaning reform – i.e., the One who reforms the affairs of creatures, for He is the One who joins every broken thing; and from this is 'setting a bone' – i.e., He repaired it. And it is said: from jabr meaning coercion – it is said: the ruler compelled him to such-and-such and forced him when he overpowered him – i.e., He compels His creatures and forces them to what He wills. So its reference on both meanings is an active attribute. And it is said: its meaning is inapproachable, unattainable – for He, glorified and exalted, is too exalted for the hand of thoughts to reach Him or the perception of sights to encompass Him. And from this is a tall palm tree (jabbāra) when it is long and hands fall short of reaching its top. So its reference is to an additive attribute (ṣifa idāfiyya) combined with a negative one. And it is said: He does not care about what has been and what has not been. And this meaning is sometimes expressed as that He does not wish for what is not and does not regret what has not been. So its reference is to the negative attributes. And it is said: He is al-‘Aẓīm (the Magnificent) – thus transmitted from Ibn ‘Abbās. Then the author interpreted al-‘Aẓīm by his saying: i.e., the attributes of deficiency are negated from Him, so its reference is a negative attribute. And it is said: i.e., those attributes are negated from Him and all attributes of perfection obtain for Him, so it returns to the negative and positive attributes together. Al-Mutakabbir (the Majestic): it is said in its meaning what was said in the meaning of al-‘Aẓīm. And al-Ghazālī (may Allah have mercy on him) said: The absolutely Majestic is the one in relation to whose essence everything sees itself as insignificant. If this vision is true, then the majesty is true and its possessor is truthful, and this is not absolutely except for Allah. And if it is false, then the majesty is false and the one claiming it is a liar. Al-Khāliq (the Creator) and al-Bāri’ (the Maker): their meaning is one – i.e., the One specifically characterized by inventing things. Al-Muṣawwir (the Fashioner): the One specifically characterized by producing the various forms and different compositions. So these three names are attributes of act. Al-Ghazālī (may Allah have mercy on him) said: It may be thought that these three are synonymous and that they refer to creation and invention. But the better way is to say: That which comes from non-existence into existence needs firstly estimation (taqdīr), secondly bringing into existence (ījād) in accordance with that estimation, and thirdly forming and adorning (taṣwīr and tazyīn), like a building by the capability of the engineer, then the builder builds it, then the decorator decorates it. So Allah, glorified, is Khāliq (Creator) in that He is the Estimer (muqaddir), and Bāri’ (Maker) in that He is the Bringer-into-existence (mūjid), and Muṣawwir (Fashioner) in that He arranges the forms of created things in the best arrangement and adorns them with the most complete adornment.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage is a lexical and theological commentary on several divine names, explaining their meanings and classifying the resulting attributes. The commentator begins with the name al-‘Azīz (the Almighty). He presents multiple linguistic interpretations: some take it as negation of parenthood or being lowered, others as invincibility or incomparability. He traces its derivation from ‘izzah (might) and notes that most interpretations lead to a negative attribute (ṣifa salbiyya), i.e., negating deficiency, though one interpretation (relating to rewarding or tormenting) makes it an active attribute (ṣifa fi‘liyya). He also mentions the view that it means al-Qādir (the Powerful), connecting ‘izzah to power and dominance. Next, he treats al-Jabbār (the Compeller) with two main interpretations: one from jabr as reform (the Restorer of broken things), and another from jabr as coercion (the One who compels creatures to His will). Both yield an active attribute. A third interpretation makes it negative (inapproachable), and a fourth makes it an additive-negative attribute. He also connects it to al-‘Aẓīm (the Magnificent) via Ibn ‘Abbās, which the author (al-Jurjānī) takes as a negative attribute or combined negative-positive. For al-Mutakabbir (the Majestic), he echoes the meaning of al-‘Aẓīm and adds al-Ghazālī’s explanation: absolute majesty is only true for Allah, as everything else is truly insignificant in relation to Him. Finally, he discusses three names: al-Khāliq (Creator), al-Bāri’ (Maker), and al-Muṣawwir (Fashioner). He notes they are active attributes and cites al-Ghazālī to differentiate them: creation involves three stages—estimation (taqdīr), bringing into existence (ījād), and forming/adornment (taṣwīr). Thus, al-Khāliq is the Estimator, al-Bāri’ is the Bringer-into-existence, and al-Muṣawwir is the Fashioner of forms in the best manner. This passage shows the careful attention to linguistic roots and theological categories in defining the divine names.

Key Terms
الجبار
صفة فعلية
صفة سلبية
صفة إضافية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think 'al-Jabbar' only means 'the Compeller' in the sense of coercion.
Correction: The passage shows it also means 'the Restorer' (reform) and 'the Inaccessible', among other meanings.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which interpretation of al-Jabbar is classified as an additive attribute (sifa idafiyya) combined with a negative one?
A) The Compeller (from jabr as coercion)
B) The Restorer (from jabr as reform)
C) The Inapproachable (manī‘)
D) The Magnificent (al-‘Aẓīm)

Key Takeaway
The name al-Jabbar encompasses meanings of restoration, compulsion, inaccessibility, and magnificence, reflecting different aspects of Allah's attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a broken relationship or a shattered hope in your life. Do you truly believe that Allah is the One who 'sets bones' and restores? What is one concrete step you can take this week to rely on al-Jabbar (the Restorer) in that situation?
?
The attribute of compulsion means Allah compels His creatures to what He wills. How does this truth affect your feeling of control over your own life? Are you resisting His will in some area? What would it look like to surrender that to Him today?
?
Allah is 'inapproachable by the hand of thoughts and the perception of sights.' Does your mental image of Allah come from His revelation or from your own imagination? What is one way you have unknowingly limited Allah in your mind, and how can you replace that with what He has revealed about Himself?

Divine Attributes
beginner
4 min
Meanings of al-Mutakabbir (المتكبر)
Al-Jurjani cites al-Ghazali's definition of al-Mutakabbir as absolute majesty based on true perception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of al-Mutakabbir, including al-Ghazali's explanation of absolute majesty.

Core Idea
Al-Mutakabbir means the One in relation to whom all else is insignificant, a true majesty only for Allah.

After al-Jabbar, Al-Jurjani turns to al-Mutakabbir, first equating it with al-Azim, then citing al-Ghazali's profound insight: true majesty is seeing everything as insignificant compared to one's own essence, which is only true for Allah. This lesson explores that concept.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on al-Mutakabbir
Read the short Arabic passage and its translation. Note that it begins by equating it with al-‘Aẓīm, then presents al-Ghazali's definition.
The passage is concise but dense.
2
Understand al-Ghazali's definition
Al-Ghazali defines absolute majesty as the state where everything sees itself as insignificant in relation to the majestic being. This perception must be true.
Only Allah meets this condition absolutely.
3
Reflect on exclusivity
Why can only Allah be al-Mutakabbir in the absolute sense? Because only He is truly such that all things are insignificant compared to Him.
This distinguishes divine majesty from human arrogance.

المرصد السابع - المقصد الثالث : تسميته تعالى بالاسماء توفيقية
وسيأتي معناه: العزيز قيل: معناه لا أب له ولا أم، وقيل: لا يحط عن منزلته، ويقرب من هذا تفسيره بالذي لا يرام أو الذي لا يخالف أو الذي لا يخوف بالتهديد، وقيل: لا مثل له، وهو بهذا المعنى وبالمعنى الأول مشتق من عز الشيء يعز بالكسر في المستقبل إذا لم يكن له نظير، ومنه عز الطعام في البلد إذا تعذر، وحاصل الكل يرجع إلى صفة سلبية. وقيل: يعذب من أراد، وقيل: عليه ثواب العاملين، فيرجع إلى صفة فعلية هي التعذيب أو الإثابة. وقيل: القادر، والعزة القدرة والغلبة. ومنه المثل: من عز، أي من قدر وغلب سلب. الجبار: قيل: من الجبر بمعنى الإصلاح، أي المصلح لأمور الخلائق فإنه جابر كل كسير، ومنه جبر العظم أي أصلحه. وقيل: من الجبر بمعنى الإكراه، يقال: جبره السلطان على كذا وأجبره إذا أكرهه، أي يجبر خلقه ويحملهم على ما يريده، فمرجعه على المعنيين صفة فعلية. وقيل: معناه منيع لا ينال، فإنه سبحانه وتعالى متعال عن أن تناله يد الأفكار أو يحيط به إدراك الأبصار، ومنه نخلة جبارة إذا طالت وقصرت الأيدي عن أن تنال أعلاها، فمرجعه إلى صفة إضافية مع سلبية. وقيل: لا يبالي بما كان وبما لم يكن، وقد يعبر عن هذا المعنى بأنه إذا لا يتمنى ما لا يكون ولا يلتهف على ما لم يكن، فمرجعه إلى الصفات السلبية. وقيل: هو العظيم، هكذا نقل عن ابن عباس، ثم فسر المصنف العظيم بقوله: أي انتفت عنه صفات النقص، فمرجعه صفة سلبية. وقيل: أي انتفى عنه تلك الصفات وحصل له جميع صفات الكمال، فيرجع إلى الصفات السلبية والثبوتية معاً. المتكبر: قيل في معناه ما قيل في معنى العظيم. وقال الغزالي رحمه الله: المتكبر المطلق هو الذي الكل يرى حقيراً بالإضافة إلى ذاته، فإن كانت هذه الرؤية صادقة كان التكبر حقاً وصاحبه محقاً، ولا ذلك على الإطلاق إلا الله، وإن كانت كاذبة كان التكبر باطلاً والمتكبر مبطلاً. الخالق البارئ معناهما واحد: أي المختص باختراع الأشياء. مقدر، وبارئ من حيث أنه موجد، ومصور من حيث أنه يرتب صور المخترعات أحسن ترتيب ويزينها أكمل تزيين.

And its meaning will come: al-‘Azīz (the Almighty) – it is said: its meaning is that He has no father nor mother, and it is said: He is not lowered from His station. Commentary
This passage is a lexical and theological commentary on several divine names, explaining their meanings and classifying the resulting attributes. The commentator begins with the name al-‘Azīz (the Almighty). He presents multiple linguistic interpretations: some take it as negation of parenthood or being lowered, others as invincibility or incomparability. Both yield an active attribute. A third interpretation makes it negative (inapproachable), and a fourth makes it an additive-negative attribute. According to al-Ghazali in the passage, when is 'takabbur' (majesty) true?
A) When the one claiming it is powerful.
B) When everything sees itself as insignificant in relation to the one claiming it, and that perception is true.
C) When the one claiming it has no rivals.
D) When the one claiming it is the creator.

?

?

?
This lesson says only Allah has true majesty. How does that truth affect the way you view your own accomplishments and status? Are there areas where you still act as if you have absolute worth independent of Allah? What step will you take to humble yourself before Him today?

Meanings of al-Khaliq, al-Bari’, al-Musawwir (الخالق، البارئ، المصور)
Al-Jurjani and al-Ghazali differentiate the three creator names by the stages of creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between the three divine names for creation: al-Khaliq, al-Bari’, and al-Musawwir, and their respective stages.

Core Idea
Creation involves three stages: estimation (taqdīr), bringing into existence (ījād), and fashioning (taṣwīr), reflected in these names.

The final part of this passage addresses three names: al-Khaliq, al-Bari’, and al-Musawwir. While they might seem synonymous, al-Ghazali distinguishes them by the stages of creation: planning, execution, and adornment. This lesson clarifies that distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on al-Khaliq, al-Bari’, and al-Musawwir
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the initial claim of synonymity between al-Khaliq and al-Bari’, then al-Ghazali's differentiation.
The analogy of the building is key.
2
Understand al-Ghazali's analogy
The building analogy: engineer (taqdīr), builder (ījād), decorator (taṣwīr). This illustrates three distinct roles.
3
Match names to stages
Al-Khaliq corresponds to the Estimator (muqaddir), al-Bari’ to the Bringer-into-existence (mūjid), al-Musawwir to the Fashioner (musawwir).
This shows these are not mere synonyms.

لا يتمنى ما لا يكون ولا يلتهف على ما لم يكن، فمرجعه إلى الصفات السلبية. وقيل: هو العظيم، هكذا نقل عن ابن عباس، ثم فسر المصنف العظيم بقوله: أي انتفت عنه صفات النقص، فمرجعه صفة سلبية. وقيل: أي انتفى عنه تلك الصفات وحصل له جميع صفات الكمال، فيرجع إلى الصفات السلبية والثبوتية معاً. المتكبر: قيل في معناه ما قيل في معنى العظيم. وقال الغزالي رحمه الله: المتكبر المطلق هو الذي الكل يرى حقيراً بالإضافة إلى ذاته، فإن كانت هذه الرؤية صادقة كان التكبر حقاً وصاحبه محقاً، ولا ذلك على الإطلاق إلا الله، وإن كانت كاذبة كان التكبر باطلاً والمتكبر مبطلاً. الخالق البارئ معناهما واحد: أي المختص باختراع الأشياء. المصور: المختص بإحداث الصور المختلفة والتراكيب المتفاوتة، فهذه الأسماء الثلاثة صفات من الفعل. قال الغزالي رحمه الله: قد يظن أن هذه الثلاثة مترادفة وأنها راجعة إلى الخلق والاختراع، والأولى أن يقال: ما يخرج من العدم إلى الوجود يحتاج أولاً إلى التقدير، وثانياً إلى الإيجاد على وفق ذلك التقدير، وثالثاً التصوير والتزيين، كالبناء بقدرة المهندس ثم يبنيه الباني ثم يزينه النقاش. فالله سبحانه خالق من حيث أنه مقدر، وبارئ من حيث أنه موجد، ومصور من حيث أنه يرتب صور المخترعات أحسن ترتيب ويزينها أكمل تزيين.
The Seventh Observatory - The Third Objective: His naming (Exalted is He) with the names is tawfīqī (subject to divine prescription). And its meaning will come: al-‘Azīz (the Almighty) – it is said: its meaning is that He has no father nor mother, and it is said: He is not lowered from His station. And close to this is its interpretation as the one who is not attained, or the one who does not oppose, or the one who does not frighten with threat. And it is said: there is no likeness to Him. And with this meaning and with the first meaning, it is derived from ‘azza al-shay’ ya‘izzu (in the future, with kasra) when it has no peer. And from this is the scarcity of food in the country when it becomes difficult. And the sum of all returns to a negative attribute (ṣifa salbiyya). And it is said: He torments whomever He wills, and it is said: upon Him is the reward of the doers of good, so it returns to an active attribute (ṣifa fi‘liyya) which is torment or reward. And it is said: al-Qādir (the Powerful), and al-‘izza is power and dominance. And from this is the proverb: 'man ‘azza' – i.e., whoever prevails and dominates, overwhelms. Al-Jabbār (the Compeller): it is said: from jabr meaning reform – i.e., the One who reforms the affairs of creatures, for He is the One who joins every broken thing; and from this is 'setting a bone' – i.e., He repaired it. And it is said: from jabr meaning coercion – it is said: the ruler compelled him to such-and-such and forced him when he overpowered him – i.e., He compels His creatures and forces them to what He wills. So its reference on both meanings is an active attribute. And it is said: its meaning is inapproachable, unattainable – for He, glorified and exalted, is too exalted for the hand of thoughts to reach Him or the perception of sights to encompass Him. And from this is a tall palm tree (jabbāra) when it is long and hands fall short of reaching its top. So its reference is to an additive attribute (ṣifa idāfiyya) combined with a negative one. And it is said: He does not care about what has been and what has not been. And this meaning is sometimes expressed as that He does not wish for what is not and does not regret what has not been. So its reference is to the negative attributes. And it is said: He is al-‘Aẓīm (the Magnificent) – thus transmitted from Ibn ‘Abbās. Then the author interpreted al-‘Aẓīm by his saying: i.e., the attributes of deficiency are negated from Him, so its reference is a negative attribute. And it is said: i.e., those attributes are negated from Him and all attributes of perfection obtain for Him, so it returns to the negative and positive attributes together. Al-Mutakabbir (the Majestic): it is said in its meaning what was said in the meaning of al-‘Aẓīm. And al-Ghazālī (may Allah have mercy on him) said: The absolutely Majestic is the one in relation to whose essence everything sees itself as insignificant. If this vision is true, then the majesty is true and its possessor is truthful, and this is not absolutely except for Allah. And if it is false, then the majesty is false and the one claiming it is a liar. Al-Khāliq (the Creator) and al-Bāri’ (the Maker): their meaning is one – i.e., the One specifically characterized by inventing things. Al-Muṣawwir (the Fashioner): the One specifically characterized by producing the various forms and different compositions. So these three names are attributes of act. Al-Ghazālī (may Allah have mercy on him) said: It may be thought that these three are synonymous and that they refer to creation and invention. But the better way is to say: That which comes from non-existence into existence needs firstly estimation (taqdīr), secondly bringing into existence (ījād) in accordance with that estimation, and thirdly forming and adorning (taṣwīr and tazyīn), like a building by the capability of the engineer, then the builder builds it, then the decorator decorates it. So Allah, glorified, is Khāliq (Creator) in that He is the Estimer (muqaddir), and Bāri’ (Maker) in that He is the Bringer-into-existence (mūjid), and Muṣawwir (Fashioner) in that He arranges the forms of created things in the best arrangement and adorns them with the most complete adornment.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage is a lexical and theological commentary on several divine names, explaining their meanings and classifying the resulting attributes. The commentator begins with the name al-‘Azīz (the Almighty). He presents multiple linguistic interpretations: some take it as negation of parenthood or being lowered, others as invincibility or incomparability. He traces its derivation from ‘izzah (might) and notes that most interpretations lead to a negative attribute (ṣifa salbiyya), i.e., negating deficiency, though one interpretation (relating to rewarding or tormenting) makes it an active attribute (ṣifa fi‘liyya). He also mentions the view that it means al-Qādir (the Powerful), connecting ‘izzah to power and dominance. Next, he treats al-Jabbār (the Compeller) with two main interpretations: one from jabr as reform (the Restorer of broken things), and another from jabr as coercion (the One who compels creatures to His will). Both yield an active attribute. A third interpretation makes it negative (inapproachable), and a fourth makes it an additive-negative attribute. He also connects it to al-‘Aẓīm (the Magnificent) via Ibn ‘Abbās, which the author (al-Jurjānī) takes as a negative attribute or combined negative-positive. For al-Mutakabbir (the Majestic), he echoes the meaning of al-‘Aẓīm and adds al-Ghazālī’s explanation: absolute majesty is only true for Allah, as everything else is truly insignificant in relation to Him. Finally, he discusses three names: al-Khāliq (Creator), al-Bāri’ (Maker), and al-Muṣawwir (Fashioner). He notes they are active attributes and cites al-Ghazālī to differentiate them: creation involves three stages—estimation (taqdīr), bringing into existence (ījād), and forming/adornment (taṣwīr). Thus, al-Khāliq is the Estimator, al-Bāri’ is the Bringer-into-existence, and al-Muṣawwir is the Fashioner of forms in the best manner. This passage shows the careful attention to linguistic roots and theological categories in defining the divine names.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think al-Khāliq, al-Bāri’, and al-Muṣawwir are perfect synonyms.
Correction: Al-Ghazālī explains they correspond to different aspects of creation: estimation, bringing into existence, and fashioning.

Checkpoint
According to al-Ghazālī in the passage, what does the name al-Khāliq specifically refer to?
A) Bringing into existence (ījād)
B) Forming and adorning (taṣwīr)
C) Estimation (taqdīr)
D) The actual building process

Key Takeaway
The names al-Khāliq, al-Bāri’, and al-Muṣawwir refer to the three stages of creation: estimation, execution, and beautification.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly see your life as the product of Allah's exact estimation (taqdīr), or do you slip into thinking things happen randomly? What decisive step today can you take to align with His taqdīr for you?
?
If al-Bāri’ brings everything into existence exactly as He estimated, then nothing about your current situation is a mistake. How does this reshape your reaction to a recent difficulty you faced?
?
Al-Muṣawwir adorns creation with perfect form. Look at your own physical form or a talent you have. How can you use that adornment to worship Him today, rather than being proud or negligent?
